Johnsen on the Achievements of Anhui Province and Wuhan Work Relief 44

Mr. Johnsen, the deputy chaplain of the English Candeburg Church, is highly regarded. He came to China from England to inspect the disaster situation. In February, he went to the disaster area of Anhui Province to inspect. In late March, he transferred to Wuhan. Recently, he returned east on the same ship as the League of Nations Investigation Team. He arrived in Shanghai yesterday. He stated that the work relief in Anhui Province and Wuhan is progressing very well, everywhere reflecting the meticulous organization and proper management of the National Government's Flood Relief Work. Although work relief has been implemented in Anhui Province, cases of starvation or suicide among disaster victims are still heard of from time to time. The inconvenience of transportation in this area makes it difficult to transport relief wheat. Recently, the National Government Disaster Relief Association adopted the method of exchanging wheat and selling wheat, which has proven effective. The Wuhan work relief has a very good impact on the security of the area, because the disaster victims have relief wheat to maintain their livelihoods and are not easily incited by Communist and reactionary elements. Mr. Johnsen has telegraphed the results of this inspection to people in his country, widely publicizing it, and deeply hopes that all sectors will actively contribute to complete China's relief work. He is scheduled to leave for northern Anhui on the 11th to inspect and participate in the opening ceremony of the newly built northern Anhui Canal.

A Heinous Crime Amidst National Crisis: A Woman With Severed Feet Swindles 45

Claiming to join the frontline in the Dachang battle, but lacking both feet, unexpectedly swindling four yuan, and smoking opium in the hotel. Mr. Zhang Yueru, an executive of the China Philanthropic and Child Welfare Association, was passing near Zhao Jiaqiao on Hart Road, Avenue Haig, at around 8 PM last night, when he suddenly saw a young woman sitting by the roadside with both feet severed. The woman appeared to be about thirty years old, fashionably dressed, speaking with a northern accent, and crying on the ground. Passersby gathered around to watch. An inquisitive person asked about her background. The woman cried and sobbed, claiming to be from Chongqing, Sichuan, and had studied at Yenching University in Peiping. During this Japanese invasion of Shanghai, she and several comrades resolutely joined the volunteer army and rushed to Shanghai to kill the enemy. Unexpectedly, in the Dachang battle, she sacrificed both feet, and several comrades who came with her died. The remaining two also had broken legs and arms. The three of them are now stranded in a hotel, and their funds have run out. They will starve to death. Today, she came here to visit a classmate surnamed Zhang to ask for a loan, but the classmate had moved to another place and could not be found. Therefore, she was wandering on the roadside, feeling unbearable sorrow. While speaking, tears fell like rain, which made the listeners feel compassion. Mr. Zhang asked where her hotel was. She said it was Anle Hotel in Taiyuanfang, Caishi Street, in the French Concession, room number 15. Mr. Zhang felt that her words were contradictory, so he invited her to go to the hotel to investigate and promised to help. However, the woman claimed that it was getting late and that she was a woman and felt it was inconvenient. She said he could do her a favor tomorrow. At that time, Wu Zong, a resident of 1215 Hetaifang, gave her four yuan and asked her to take it. The woman pretended to be shy but accepted it impolitely and put it in her arms, hiring a car and leaving proudly. Mr. Zhang became suspicious, so at around 10 PM, he went to Anle Hotel to inquire. The hotel's tea waiter said that there was no woman with severed feet staying in the hotel. Mr. Zhang left and went to the neighboring Tongle Hotel to ask the tea waiters. Unexpectedly, there was indeed a woman with severed feet staying in room number seven, living there for several months, counting the time even before the January 28th incident. She had been without feet since she arrived, living quite luxuriously and having savings in the bank. Mr. Zhang did not wait for him to finish speaking and rushed to push open the door. Unexpectedly, when the door opened, he saw the woman with severed feet lying on the bed, frequently playing a short flute, and the smell of opium enveloping the entire room. The woman was panicked when she suddenly saw Mr. Zhang. The short flute was in her hand, making it difficult to blow it or throw it away. At this point, Mr. Zhang did not bother to ask more questions and left angrily. He reported it to the reporter that night. Alas, in this ten-mile foreign concession, everything is strange. The woman with severed feet can use the national crisis and her own shortcomings to create a new trick. It can be said that she is cunning.

Conspiring to Kill His Wife 46

The great number of life and death... the wife was rescued. The three accomplices... were all arrested. Ge Chengrong, a Yangzhou native who was a foreman on the Longda ship at the Datong Wharf, is now fifty years old. On March 2nd at 8 AM, he allegedly conspired with his fellow villager Dong Shaoqing and others to murder his wife, Ge Chenshi (49 years old, Yangzhou native). The other day, Chinese detectives Lang Jintang and Bao Qiu Sijiu, and Western detective Smith of the Lao Zha Police Station arrested Ge and Dong. Yesterday morning, they were escorted to the Criminal Division of the First Special District Local Court, where Judge Zhou Hanting presided over the interrogation. First, the police lawyer Ru Bao Yi stated that the Public Works Bureau is prosecuting according to Article 282, Section 2 of the Criminal Law for murder. If the written interrogation reveals premeditated behavior by the defendant, the legal article will be changed. Lawyer Ru also detailed the circumstances of the case, stating that the victim, Ge Chenshi, and the defendant, Ge Chengrong, are formally married. Five years ago, they developed animosity, and Ge took Zhao as a concubine. Because she was not tolerated by the legal wife, Ge and Zhao lived together at 43 Sanyuanfang, Yangshupu. Ge was previously a foreman on the Longda ship, and then transferred the foreman position to Ge Chenshi to continue. Ge became unemployed. For five years, life has been difficult. He wanted to regain the foreman position, but there was no suitable opportunity. Recently, he learned that Ge Chenshi was having an affair with Liu Ruyuan, which made him feel burning anger. He wanted to find a way to slander her. At that time, Dong Shaoqing, a tailor from the same village who could not operate due to the war, came to Shanghai to seek employment from Ge. Ge discussed this matter with Dong, saying that if he could help him regain the foreman position, he could help him there in the future. So, on February 28th of this year, at 2 PM, at the Tongchun Garden Teahouse on Dongxinqiao Street in the French Concession, Ge invited Lao Cui (who is at large) and Wu Xiaodaizi, and Dong, four people to discuss how to put Ge Chenshi to death. Since she was a woman and unable to resist, they decided to use violence. On March 2nd, at 6 AM, the four of them went to Ge Chenshi's home at 57 Hongruili, Xinzha Road, and divided the work. Lao Cui waited downstairs. Ge, Dong, and Wu went upstairs and entered her bedroom in the back building. But since it was early in the morning, she was still asleep and not awake. Since the maid Zhang Shenshi was also in the room, fearing that it would hinder their work, they ordered Shenshi to go out to brew water and asked her to buy pan-fried buns from the shop to prolong the time, making it easier to work. Ge opened and closed the door and hid behind the door. Dong went forward and grabbed Ge Chenshi's throat with his hand, trying to strangle her to death. At first, he saw her feet still moving and tried his best to strangle her. Later, seeing that she was still, he thought she was dead and hurriedly fled. At this time, the maid Zhang Shenshi also returned, witnessing the situation in shock, and tried to save Ge Chenshi, who was able to wake up. She immediately reported to the Xinzha Police Station, saying that she had been murdered by her husband and three or two people whose names she did not know. The police investigation revealed that the unknown people were Dong Shaoqing and Wu Xiaodaizi. As for Lao Cui, the plaintiff did not know because he was downstairs. Until yesterday morning, the plaintiff met Dong on Laohe Road and reported him to the police, who arrested him and revealed the instigator, Ge Chengrong, who was arrested at 3 Sanyuanfang Road, Yangshupu. However, Ge denied everything in the police station, and Dong also claimed that Wu Xiaodaizi did it. However, the victim, Ge Chenshi, identified Dong Shaoqing as the one who did it in the police station. Her confession was recorded and presented to the court for investigation. Furthermore, Chinese detective Lang Jintang testified that when he went to Ge's house to arrest him yesterday, Ge Chengrong was hiding under the firewood pile under the bed and was dragged out by him. The victim Ge Chenshi also stated that Ge Chengrong is my husband. Five years ago, we had a lawsuit because he took a concubine and signed an agreement to separate and have nothing to do with each other. The so-called Liu Ruyuan is not my lover, but an accountant who has returned to his hometown of Yangzhou. On March 2nd, at 7 AM, Ge, Dong, and others arrived one after another. When I asked them what they were doing, they prevaricated each other. After a while, Ge closed the door and Dong grabbed my throat with both hands. Another person knelt on my chest and pressed down on my legs. At that time, I shouted for help. Dong said, "Today I will take your life." After a while, I felt confused. I seemed to hear Dong say, "She's dead, she's dead." He also said, "We should have come a long time ago, but you have lived a few days longer." Later, the maid came and rescued me, reported to the police station, and sent me to the hospital, where I stayed for four or five days before returning home to recuperate. Furthermore, the witness, maid Zhang Shenshi, testified to everything. When questioned, the defendant Dong Shaoqing confessed that he was instructed by Ge to go with him, but he was also downstairs, and Wu Xiaodaizi did it. When questioned, Ge Chengrong denied the allegations, saying that the facts were false accusations. Judge Zhou verified the confessions and ordered the case to be adjourned for seven days for further interrogation. The defendants were returned to custody separately.

Gong Linan Wounded by an Enemy 50

Gong Linan, a Henan native, is now twenty years old and lives at 1024 Sanyili, Yangzhou Road, Yangshupu. He is a worker at the Hengfeng Cotton Mill. Yesterday afternoon at around 5 PM, while walking on Huacheng Road, he suddenly encountered three people. One of them held an axe and, without asking why, struck Gong hard on the back with the axe, causing a wound about three or four inches deep. He immediately fell to the ground in extreme pain, and blood gushed out like a spring. The assailant, seeing that his goal had been achieved, left. He was sent to Tongren Hospital for treatment by police car number 2314.

Two Lost Children 51

Gu Gendi and Lan Ying. At around 10 PM the other night, two girls got lost in the Hujunying area of Nanshi. One child was wearing a cheongsam vest made of flowered foreign cloth, flowered socks, yellow leather shoes, a monk's haircut, and a pink flannel hat. The other child was wearing a short shirt and pants made of flowered foreign cloth, flowered cloth shoes, two braids, and a pair of silver bracelets on her hands. They were taken to the First Section of the First District by the patrol police. According to one child, her name is Gu Gendi, seven years old, from Chongming. The other child's name is Lan Ying, six years old. The rest she could not say. They were ordered to stay and wait for their family members to claim them.

Tan Ayou Says It Is Better to Die Than Be a Slave of a Conquered Nation 52

Tan Ayou, a Cantonese, used to work as a stoker on a ship. His life was not difficult. After the Shanghai war broke out, Tan often had endless feelings of emotion, writing in the air and saying that he would become a slave of a conquered nation. Until the Chinese army retreated, Tan became more and more saddened and often said that it was better to die than to be a slave of a conquered nation. Yesterday morning, Tan attempted suicide by throwing himself into the river, but was rescued by Xue Silin and sent to the Water Patrol Police Station for transfer to the Local Court for placement.

Public Security Bureau Pays Attention to Public Security 53

Checking Household Registration. The Shanghai County Government, considering that the overall situation is not yet stable and fearing that unscrupulous people may be hiding in the territory and disrupting public security, ordered the Public Security Bureau to pay close attention. After receiving the order, the Bureau immediately ordered all sub-bureaus to report on residents moving, changing addresses, and relatives and friends staying overnight at any time, so that police could conduct on-site investigations to ensure local security and maintain public order.

Confiscated a Huge Amount of Red Pills 54

Estimated at 300 Pounds. Chen Wenbing, a dock porter, was hired by the Liyuan Shipping Bureau at 35 Huangpu Bund, French Concession, on the evening of the 25th of last month, to carry two sacks of poisonous red pills, weighing 47 pounds, intending to send them to the Jiangtian Steamboat. He was intercepted by Chinese patrolman number 236 of the French Police and taken into custody. That night, detective supervisor Chen Sanlin and detectives of the day shift searched four bags of the same poisonous pills in the kitchen shed of the Shipping Bureau, weighing 250 pounds. The owner of the bureau, Tang Weibing, had already fled beforehand. The clerk Zhang Meichu, Fang Furu, and apprentice Zhang Hanjin were taken into custody and sent to the Second Special District Court, prosecuted under Article 6 of the Anti-Smoking Law, and detained pending trial. This case was twice examined by Judge Li Changnian, who declared the辩论 closed and scheduled a date for sentencing. Yesterday was the sentencing date. At 2 PM, Judge Li presided over the Criminal Division and ordered the defendants to be brought to court. Zhang Meichu and Fang Furu were sentenced to six months in prison each for the crime of helping to sell opium substitutes, and fined 2,400 yuan each. If the fines could not be paid through forced execution, the sentence would be commuted to one day of imprisonment for every three yuan. Chen Wenbing and Zhang Hanjin were found not guilty. The 47 pounds and 250 pounds of red pills were confiscated.

Child Burned to Death in Caojiadu 55

Yesterday (the 9th) at 11:15 AM, a fire broke out at the home of the Chen family at 6 Hongxingli, Jilifeier Road, Caojiadu, due to cooking lunch. The fire quickly spread, and thick smoke billowed through the roof. Fortunately, a patrolman noticed it and reported it to the fire brigade, who rushed to the scene and extinguished the fire. However, the Chen family's two-year-old boy, who was sleeping upstairs, could not be rescued in time and was burned to death. A total of two floors were burned down. The Sixth District Police Department sent police to investigate the cause of the fire and detained the fire master, Chen Shunhe (28 years old, from Yuyao), pending investigation.

Thugs Extort Money Outside the Benevolent Hall 56

Sentenced to 40 Days of Detention. The Tongren Fuyuan Branch Hall on Ningbo Road in the French Concession specializes in collecting and burying exposed or abandoned coffins and corpses found on the streets. Also, if the families of deceased children in the city have no place to bury them after encoffining them, they can be sent to the hall for burial. Unexpectedly, thugs often wait outside the back door of the hall, and when they see someone carrying a small coffin there, they extort money from them, treating it as a source of profit. Although the hall has repeatedly reported this to the police station, which has sent detectives to arrest and detain them, the thugs do not repent and continue to extort money as before. On the 28th of last month, at noon, someone carried a small coffin to the hall, asking for it to be buried. Local thugs Wang Changsheng and three accomplices extorted five yuan from the people carrying the coffin, claiming that they had to pay at least 2.4 yuan, calling it "toll money." They were threatening and prevented the hall staff from receiving the coffin. The hall staff believed that such unlawful behavior was hindering charitable acts, so they telephoned the Great Clock Police Station, which sent detectives Gu Mingzhou and Lu Jinnan to arrest them. The accomplices had fled, but they arrested Li and took him to the Second Special District Court, prosecuting him under the charges of intimidation and fraud, and detaining him pending trial. Judge Li Changnian examined the case. The defendant's confession was cunning, but the witness, a hall staff member, testified. The court found the case clear and declared the trial closed. Yesterday at 2 PM, Judge Li presided over the Criminal Division and ordered Wang Changsheng to be brought to court, sentencing the defendant to 40 days of detention for the crime of intimidation and extortion. The number of days of detention before the sentence was finalized was deducted at a rate of one day of detention for every two days.

City Chamber of Commerce Sends Letter to Various Industries Requesting Advances 59

The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce yesterday sent letters to various industry associations, saying that as a result of the Northeast Incident and the Shanghai War, it is necessary to exert all efforts on international publicity, resulting in printing, postal, and advertising expenses exceeding the budget. Weather Report 61

The Xujiahui Observatory's weather forecast at 4:30 PM yesterday stated that the coastal area here would have cloudy weather with signs of change, and the Yangtze River basin would have fog due to a low pressure system forming in southwestern China. The Shandong coast would have northeasterly winds, and the Ma'an Island and southern areas would have easterly winds. Also, in the 24 hours before 3:00 PM yesterday, the highest temperature in this port was 68.0, and the lowest was 45.9. On the same day last year, the highest was 64.2, and the lowest was 32.7.

It was verified and confirmed that he should be immediately dismissed as a disciplinary measure. This order was to be obeyed. (Signed) Wen Yingxing, Bureau Chief. (Signed) Qi Haitian.

Because they were busy, all public banquets were declined, only agreeing to attend Zhang's banquet on the evening of the 10th. After the investigation is completed, they will go to Nara to compile a report. However, who is responsible for protecting the trains traveling from Beiping to Shenyang outside the pass is still under negotiation. (Special Dispatch from the 9th)

Supplementary Record of Lytton's Speech in Jinan 67

(Jinan) Zhang Honglie, Director of the Construction Department, gave a welcoming speech on behalf of Han [Fuqu] to the League of Nations investigation team, saying that the provincial government and the people were very honored to gather with the gentlemen of the League of Nations investigation team. Chairman Han was unable to come due to illness, and he was very sorry, so he ordered me to say a few words on his behalf. The gentlemen have come from afar and have visited Shanghai, and I believe that all the circumstances are clear. When passing through Beijing, you met with the central government, and I believe the gentlemen are also clear about the central government's hopes. Today, the gentlemen come to Shandong, which has been a land of peace and justice for thousands of years in China. Confucius was born in this land. His lifelong teachings emphasized loyalty, filial piety, trustworthiness, righteousness, love, and peace. Therefore, the people of Shandong most believe in benevolence, concession, and peace. Only benevolence, concession, and peace can eliminate those who are not peaceful and concessionary. The reason why the world can be peaceful lies in the point of peace and concession. The gentlemen of your team are envoys of peace and are responsible for resolving the Sino-Japanese dispute. The Chinese people deeply believe that the gentlemen can resolve the Sino-Japanese dispute without a doubt. I welcome you on behalf of Chairman Han and wish you a smooth and complete success in the future. At this point, he raised his glass in salute, and Li Zhifan, Director of the Salt Affairs Inspection Office, translated. Lytton listened, looked up at the ceiling, and pondered deeply. Then, amidst applause, he gave a reply, which was still translated by Li, saying that he was very honored to gather with everyone today, but he was very sad to hear that Chairman Han was ill, and asked him to convey this message. Just now, Director Zhang spoke on behalf of Chairman Han, saying that the people of Shandong do not hope that our team will show great compassion, but hope that we will handle the matter impartially. Our team visited various tragic situations in Shanghai, which need not be detailed. When we make a report to the League of Nations in the future, it will not be to report the tragic sights we have seen, but to report the atmosphere of peace everywhere. When our team gathered in New York, many Americans had unlimited hopes for our team. In Japan and China, there are many welcomers everywhere, and there is an atmosphere of seeking peace everywhere, unlike those who have hatred. Our team represents 54 countries and does not want any two countries to have war. Seeing that everyone hopes for peace, we hope to use the peaceful psychology of the majority to restrain those who are not peaceful. At this point, he raised his glass in response. Regarding the questions raised by the Jinan press, 1) What is your opinion on the Shanghai ceasefire conference? Lytton said that it has been satisfactorily answered. I see that everyone hopes for peace, which will surely help the permanent peace between China and Japan. 2) How has the investigation of the war zones in Shanghai and your understanding of China been? Lytton said that Shandong is the hometown of Confucius. Thousands of years before the League of Nations was established, Confucius's teachings were already very beneficial to the world. Now, we should study and maintain world peace based on Confucius's teachings. (Special Dispatch from the 9th)

League of Nations Special Committee to Reconvene Tomorrow 108

A Fierce Debate Expected on the Shanghai Case Reuters Geneva, 9th The arrangements have now been made here for a very important discussion next week, consisting of four matters: the stalemate in the Far East and the Danube, the Disarmament Conference, and international labor affairs. Delegations will arrive here successively at the end of this week. British Foreign Secretary Simon is scheduled to arrive here by plane tomorrow. It is expected that when the Special Committee of 19 nations elected by the League of Nations General Assembly reconvenes to discuss the Sino-Japanese dispute, there will be another fierce debate, because China has now expressed dissatisfaction with the slow progress of the Shanghai negotiations. The new plan proposed by Japan makes the withdrawal of Japanese troops conditional on guarantees of the safety of the lives, property, and legitimate businesses of Japanese residents in Shanghai, which League of Nations officials regard as vague and likely to lead to endless prevarication. It is expected that when the Special Committee meets, the Chinese delegation will do its utmost to ask the League of Nations to exert moral pressure on Japan, ordering it to abandon this plan and determine a date for the withdrawal of troops.

Stimson to Travel to Europe with Kellogg 109

Reuters New York, 8th US Secretary of State Stimson and former Secretary of State Kellogg, the initiator of the Non-Aggression Pact, set off for Europe today. Stimson will temporarily serve as the US Chief Delegate to the Geneva Disarmament Conference. After boarding the ship, when asked whether the US would be unwilling to reduce its military spending while Japanese troops had not withdrawn from Northeast China, Stimson replied that this statement was not true and that he hoped the Sino-Japanese dispute could be resolved without causing war in the Far East. Kellogg also went to Geneva to attend the League of Nations conference.

National News New York, 8th According to Stimson, there are several proposals in Geneva that have a good chance of reaching an agreement, and these proposals should tend to reduce the chances of war. It is heard that Stimson will first go to Geneva, and then visit London and other European capitals. Although the purpose of this trip is to promote disarmament, it is said that Stimson really wants to talk to European politicians about Far Eastern policy, especially regarding the Sino-Japanese dispute.

Havas Washington, 8th After Stimson goes to Europe, he will meet with diplomatic authorities from various countries. US political figures have indicated that Stimson will get those countries with interests in the Far East to reach an understanding on the economic side. Stimson will also find out what methods European countries will take if Japan's ambitions expand in China to ensure the Kellogg-Briand Pact and what attitudes European countries intend to adopt towards the future status of the puppet state of Manchuria and the current situation in Shanghai, which Stimson also wants to understand.

Italian and German Newspapers Voice Criticism

National News Agency Rome, 8th The failure of the London Four-Power Conference does not surprise the political circles here, because based on the resolute attitude of France, it was expected that it would be difficult to have results. Important News

British Comment on Anglo-American-Japanese Triangular Diplomatic Relations 117

Britain Should Cooperate with the United States to Maintain Peace in the Pacific Tokyo Asahi Shimbun carried a dispatch from its London correspondent, saying that the well-known commentator Wickham Steed has published an essay on British policy in the Pacific, detailing Britain's position of pacifism supported by the League of Nations. The British government should cooperate with the United States to safeguard the international peace treaty, and to maintain peace in the Pacific and seek the security of the British Empire, it has no choice but to cooperate with the United States. The first half of his essay observes Japan, saying that based on the impression of reactionary Japanese people that Steed obtained in the United States in 1921, it is a big question whether Japanese diplomats and politicians can determine Japan's policy or not. Recalling the World War, at the Washington Preparatory Conference, Prime Minister George and Foreign Minister Kato both argued that the United Kingdom should adopt a detached position on the survival of the Anglo-Japanese alliance due to the US-Japan dispute. Because the interests of the United Kingdom are contrary to those of Japan, even if the US and Japan go to war, the United Kingdom cannot participate, but part of the British Empire will inevitably be involved in the vortex, because Japan's provocative policy is that all English-speaking people are hostile to Japan. Judging from the secret opinion submitted to the naval authorities in 1921, Japan at that time had a superior naval power and was likely to induce war. At that time, the naval authorities of Britain and the United States both believed that Japan would expel the US Navy from the Pacific and occupy Honolulu and the Philippines within a few months. On the one hand, Japan will establish political and economic activities and labor in China and become the leader of the Far East. This is the only purpose that the Japanese military has always cherished. If this ambition of Japan extends to the entire Far East and Asia, wouldn't it be contrary to the interests of the United Kingdom? At that time, the United Kingdom itself cannot stand in a position of isolated closure. In terms of the meaning of the nation and race, for example, when a crisis is caused by the immigration problem, it is easier for the Japanese military to control German policy than the German military in 1914. This is Japan's high-profile Pan-Asianism and its efforts to expand its power. However, whether the policy it holds can be realized is also a question. If an incident occurs between the US and Japan one day, even if the British government wants to maintain neutrality, British Columbia will probably rise up against Japan. From this point of view, the United Kingdom's policy at the Washington Conference was quite concerned about the US-Japan dispute and urgently sought to resolve the Pacific problem. Therefore, at present, there is no other way than to unite the United States to maintain peace.

In Yamagata Prefecture, the Education Labor Department branch of the All-Association System of Reddened Groups organized by elementary school teachers has seven key figures in the extreme-left illegal movement, including Takahashi Kozo, a teacher at Kashiwakura Kadota Elementary School in Minamimurayama District, who have been vigorously promoting the Reddening of elementary school children. In addition, the Daikan-yama Police Station detected an unstable group gathering and plotting at the Reimei Society in Kojimachi Ward, and successively arrested left-wing elements centered on various employment agencies throughout the city.

The Proletarian Cultural League, as the center of the extreme-left Shanghai Movement, has been quite active recently. It has now been revealed by Professor Yamada Katsujiro and his wife of Kyoto Imperial University that they have a capital of more than 10,000 yuan, and have organized six groups: the Alliance of Proletarian Writers, the Proletarian Left-Wing Theater, Proletarian Art, and photography, film, and music. They have united six groups, including the Japanese Proletarian Science Research Institute, the New Education Research Institute, the Militant Atheist League, the Proletarian Birth Restriction League, the Japanese Proletarian Library, and the Japanese Proletarian Esperanto League, to form the Japanese Proletarian Cultural Grand Alliance. The Alliance headquarters is located in Kanda Ward, Mandai-cho, and its organ is called Red Flag. After the police station obtained the confession, they immediately arrested more than a dozen important figures, including the Central Secretary-General of the Cultural League, Viscount Okouchi Masatoshi's son, Okouchi Nobutake, Central Standing Committee members Nomura Jiro, Terashima Kazuo, Hatano Ichiro, and Onomiya Yoshikichi. At the same time, three or forty left-wing elements, including Saegusa Kazuyasu, the executive chairman of the All-Farmers Association of Yamanashi Prefecture, were also arrested one after another. In addition, Saito Hashimoto and other Tokyo Imperial University students, members of the Communist Youth League's Tokyo Imperial University cell, who held a secret meeting at the Sanmaru Restaurant in Hongo Ward on the 30th of last month, were also arrested. Others, such as Yamada Giichi, Aoki Hajime, and dozens of other students from Waseda University, as well as Inoue, Hasegawa, and several other left-leaning female students from the Tokyo Kojimachi Women's English School, were arrested together. However, judging from the recent situation, the left-leaning movement is almost like a prairie fire. All sectors of the intellectual community are participating in the planning, so the Metropolitan Police Department is arresting people without end.

Important News 2

Guangdong Province Issues National Defense Bonds 120

The total amount of bonds is 30 million yuan. According to a Guangzhou dispatch, the Southwest Political Affairs Committee recently held a meeting and passed Chen Jitang's proposal to issue 30 million yuan of national defense bonds. The funds will be used to purchase cannons, build coastal fortresses and fortifications, and purchase aircraft. The issuance and repayment methods of the bonds were revised by the Southwest Political Affairs Committee. On the 31st of last month, the secretariat of the committee issued the revised methods to the Finance Department for preparation. It is planned to start issuing the bonds on May 1st of this year, and at the same time, start collecting surcharges to pay interest and repay the principal. Therefore, Guangdong's provincial and national taxes will be increased by one-tenth from May 1st. For example, if a certain tobacco and alcohol tax is 10 yuan, it will be collected 11 yuan from May 1st until the principal is fully repaid. The funds collected from the additional one-tenth will be handed over to the Custody Committee for safekeeping. The repayment method is to repay in 30 installments from May 1st of this year, with a lottery drawing every two months. Representatives will be sent by the Political Affairs Committee, the Provincial Government, the Finance Department, the Chamber of Commerce, and other institutions and organizations to form a Custody Committee to supervise the use of the funds. As for the method of promoting the bonds, it is scheduled to be implemented on May 1st. Stores, residents, docks, and various businesses in major cities and towns throughout the province, such as Guangzhou, Shantou, Jiangmen, and Foshan, will be allocated bonds according to one month's rent. All contractors and companies will be allocated bonds according to one month's salary. Business licenses and business taxes in various counties and cities will be allocated bonds at 2% of the capital amount. It is required to raise the full amount within 12 months from May 1st of this year. Interest will be paid once a year on May 1st, starting from 1933 (April 4th).

The Investigation Mission's Situation from Beijing to the West (3) 121

Appendix: The League of Nations' Handling of the Sino-Japanese Dispute. C. Japan's New Policy. In the past, Japan refused to withdraw its troops, arguing that the anti-Japanese sentiment among the Chinese people was very strong. Therefore, the safety of Japanese residents' lives and property should be the primary concern before withdrawing troops. Later, because the Chinese government declared that it would be responsible for protecting Japanese residents, and said that if Japan did not believe it, it could also ask neutral countries to send personnel to participate in the protection work, the problem of Japanese residents' safety was easily resolved. At this time, Japan realized that this reason was not a good plan, and changed its strategy. On October 12th, in its reply to the chairman of the Executive Yuan's advice letter of the 9th, it said that in this serious situation, the urgent task was to restore the spirit of friendship and cooperation between China and Japan. To achieve this goal, China should first recognize several basic principles to maintain the diplomatic relations between the two countries. If China can recognize these principles, Japan will be able to withdraw its troops immediately. The Japanese government is willing to start negotiations with the Chinese government at any time, etc. However, the five principles mentioned were not explained in detail, so before the meeting started, all countries knew that the matter was already tricky.

D. The Process of the Second Meeting of the Executive Yuan 122

(1) The Discussion of Inviting the United States to Attend the Meeting of the Executive Yuan. Among the important issues of this meeting was inviting the United States to send personnel to participate in the work of the Executive Yuan. Before the meeting, the British and French governments seemed to have obtained the consent of the U.S. government, and the U.S. government had also declared to the press before being formally invited that if the League of Nations invited the U.S. to participate in the meeting of the Executive Yuan, the U.S. government would gladly accept it. After this declaration was issued, the Executive Yuan was in a position where it was difficult to back down. However, Japan was most afraid of the U.S. cooperating with the League of Nations and interfering in its actions in China, so it strongly opposed it, which was expected. Therefore, the so-called constitutional issue arose.

Japan's opposition to the United States' participation was based on Article 4, Paragraph 5 of the League of Nations Covenant. That paragraph states that if a member of the League of Nations that is not on the Executive Council encounters an event that is specifically related to it when the Council discusses it, it may request that it send a representative to attend the meeting in the name of a member of the Executive Council, etc. Therefore, Japan said that according to the provisions of that treaty, only members of the League of Nations can participate in the meeting of the Executive Council. The United States is not a member of the League of Nations, so it cannot participate in the meeting of the Executive Council constitutionally. Now, the meeting of the Executive Council is based on Article 11 of the League of Nations Covenant, so even if the Executive Council wants to invite the United States to participate, it must be passed unanimously. In this way, Japan can have two ways to prevent the proposal, believing that it can definitely dispel the proposal to invite the United States. However, the representatives of various countries in the Executive Council believe that the cooperation of the United States is of great importance to the future of the League of Nations. No matter what, this goal must be achieved. When the Japanese representative sent a letter to Briand on October 15th, proposing the above-mentioned principles, Briand immediately replied that the cooperation with the United States was based on the fact that the Japanese representative had approved the resolution of September 30th, which said that the Executive Council should notify the United States of the progress of the discussion of the Sino-Japanese dispute at any time, and not based on Article 4, Paragraph 5 of the League of Nations Covenant. Therefore, the Japanese representative's opposition was a misunderstanding. He also said that if the United States is willing to send personnel to attend the meeting of the Executive Council, it will not be in the capacity of a member, because it has no voting rights. As for the issue of inviting the United States to send personnel, it is only a procedural issue, so there is no need for the Executive Council to pass it unanimously. In order to delay the time, the Japanese representative again proposed to form a committee of legal experts to discuss this constitutional issue in detail. Who knew that the British Foreign Minister immediately asked the Japanese representative that if the Executive Council established a special committee to study this legal issue, would the representative be able to accept its report in advance? Then the Japanese representative again seized the opportunity to say no. Briand then put the Japanese proposal to establish a committee of legal experts to a vote. As a result, except for the representatives of Japan and Germany, the rest opposed it. The chairman then put the original proposal to invite the United States to participate to a vote. As a result, except for the Japanese representative, everyone unanimously approved it. This was the situation of the secret meeting on October 15th. When the meeting was held on the 16th, the chairman announced that the Executive Council had decided to invite the United States to send personnel to attend the meeting of the Executive Council based on yesterday's resolution, hoping that the Japanese representative would also express his sympathy. The Japanese representative said that he could not change his previous intention. The Polish representative said that the reason why he supported the United States' attendance at the meeting of the Executive Council was because he recognized that the resolution was a separate matter and had nothing to do with the interpretation of the League of Nations Constitution. Representatives from Yugoslavia and Norway also made similar statements one after another. The intention was to recognize that this invitation to the United States to attend the meeting of the Executive Council was based on the resolution of September 30th and not based on any article of the League of Nations Covenant, so it could not be used as a precedent in the future. In fact, it was to prevent the Soviet Union from participating by analogy, because the Soviet Union is one of the major countries that are not at war and the Pacific Ocean. Its status is no different from that of the United States. A dispute ended here. When the meeting was held on the afternoon of the same day, the United States sent its consul general stationed in Geneva to attend. Representatives from various countries gave a warm welcome, but the Japanese representative remained silent. A few days later, the Japanese representative said that the reason why the Japanese government opposed the United States' attendance in the past was because of the differences in the interpretation of the League of Nations Covenant, and it had nothing to do with the United States.

(2) The Movement to Apply the Kellogg-Briand Pact. Since the U.S. representative had already attended the meeting of the Executive Council, if the application of the Kellogg-Briand Pact could not be carried out, it would lose the meaning of cooperating with the U.S. Therefore, on October 17th, representatives from various countries exchanged opinions on the application of Article 2 of the Kellogg-Briand Pact. The meaning of that article is that if signatory countries encounter disputes, regardless of the cause and nature, they should only use peaceful methods to resolve the negotiations. As a result, it was decided that the governments of various countries should instruct their diplomatic representatives stationed in China and Tokyo to advise the governments of China and Japan to strictly abide by the obligations of Article 2 of the Kellogg-Briand Pact, and the French government should notify all signatory countries of the Kellogg-Briand Pact to make the same statement. After receiving the notification from the French government, the U.S. government issued the same advice. After receiving the advice, the Chinese government replied on October 22nd, saying that China has always abided by the Kellogg-Briand Pact, and Japan is now clearly violating it. The signatory countries should immediately correct it. The Japanese government's reply also arrived on the 23rd, divided into three points: (1) It claimed that the advance into the eastern provinces was out of self-defense and denied violating the Kellogg-Briand Pact. (2) Japan wanted to resolve the Sino-Japanese dispute peacefully and was willing to negotiate directly with China. (3) It accused the Chinese government of inciting the people to carry out anti-Japanese activities.

(3) The Debate on the Japanese Air Force Bombing Jinzhou. The debate on the bombing of Jinzhou was very pleasant. When the representative of our country questioned Japan's reason for bombing Jinzhou with large aircraft, the Japanese representative said that Chinese troops were concentrating in Jinzhou to endanger the Japanese army, so the Japanese army headquarters sent aircraft to the area to investigate the situation. Because the Chinese troops fired on the Japanese aircraft, they dropped bombs in self-defense. Representative Shi said that last year, an American aircraft arrived in Tokyo. Because the entry procedures were not in compliance, it was detained by the Japanese government. Now, Japan sent military aircraft to Jinzhou. Not only were the procedures not in compliance, but they were also carrying bombs. The purpose must be known. Moreover, the Chinese army in Jinzhou has no anti-aircraft guns, which shows that the Japanese aircraft was not attacked. The Japanese army has harmed the lives and property of the Chinese people for no reason. The resolution of the Executive Council on September 30th has been completely destroyed. The Japanese representative knew that he was wrong, so he only said that his opinion was different from that of the Chinese representative and there was no need to say more. The onlookers were even more resentful and also expressed dissatisfaction with the Japanese army's actions. This was the general situation of the two meetings on October 13th.

(4) The Preparation Process of the Draft Resolution on October 22nd. From the 16th to the 22nd, representatives from various countries worked hard to draft the resolution, which was the focus of this meeting. The method was that the chairman first solicited opinions from both sides, and then discussed them with representatives from other countries, circulating back and forth, and drafting the draft based on the views of all parties. However, due to the differences in the opinions of the two sides, it was extremely difficult to carry out mediation. At that time, it was said that Briand was ill because he was exhausted from dealing with all parties, which shows his difficult situation. It is said that the draft submitted for discussion was the third revised draft because there were first and second drafts before, which were eventually abandoned. The content of the first draft took into account both direct negotiations and the deadline for troop withdrawal. Later, it was abandoned because the Japanese side opposed the deadline for troop withdrawal and our side opposed direct negotiations. The next day, rumors spread that the U.S. government opposed the deadline for troop withdrawal and was unwilling to continue cooperating with the League of Nations. Briand turned pale when he heard this and summoned neutral representatives to draft another draft, the content of which abandoned the deadline for troop withdrawal and advocated direct negotiations. After this draft was strongly opposed by Representative Shi, the British Foreign Minister received a report from his ambassador to the United States, saying that the U.S. attitude was the same as before, so the second draft was also abandoned. However, representatives from various countries realized that the meeting had been going on for a week and there was no way to change the Japanese representative's attitude. Therefore, on October 2nd, they submitted the third draft for voting. The content of the draft was divided into seven points: (1) Both parties have the obligation to abide by the resolution of September 30th. According to that resolution, Japan should withdraw its troops outside the South Manchuria Railway line in the shortest possible time, and China should use effective methods to protect the lives and property of Japanese residents. (2) Please pay attention to the previous promises of both parties not to expand the conflict and stop the invasion. (3) Please pay attention to Japan's previous declaration of not annexing Chinese land, and recognize that this declaration is in line with the League of Nations Covenant and the Nine-Power Treaty regarding respecting China's sovereignty, territorial administrative independence, and integrity. (4) Request Japan to start withdrawing its troops immediately and complete it before the Executive Council meeting on November 16th, and request the Chinese government to take effective measures to effectively protect the lives and property of Japanese residents and hire neutral countries to assist Chinese officials in implementing this resolution. (5) Suggest that the governments of China and Japan immediately send personnel to negotiate the methods of withdrawing troops and receiving lost territory. (6) Suggest that both parties, as soon as the troop withdrawal is completed, immediately conduct direct negotiations to resolve all issues related to this dispute and the Manchuria Railway. Therefore, both parties should jointly form a Sino-Japanese mediation committee or other similar institutions. (7) Decide to convene a meeting on November 16th to re-examine. If necessary, the chairman may convene the above-mentioned draft content in advance, although it may not satisfy us, but it can generally accept our country's advocacy of a deadline for troop withdrawal and rejection of direct negotiations. Diplomatically speaking, it can be said to be our country's victory. The representatives of China and Japan replied as soon as the chairman read out the case, agreeing to ask their respective governments for instructions.

(5) Japan's Counter-Proposal. At the 14th meeting on October 23rd, the representative of our country said that although the Chinese government was not satisfied with yesterday's draft, it was determined to accept it in order to resolve the Sino-Japanese dispute as soon as possible. However, the Japanese representative still firmly opposed it and put forward a counter-proposal, the content of which was divided into eight items. The first, second, and third items were the same as the first, second, and third items of the original proposal, only with differences in wording, so they will not be repeated. However, the fourth to eighth items were completely different from the original proposal. The fourth item mainly said that in order to restore the state of peace, the governments of China and Japan should be requested to recognize several basic principles for maintaining diplomatic relations between the two countries, so that the lives and property of Japanese residents can be effectively protected. The fifth item was to suggest to the governments of China and Japan to immediately start direct negotiations to realize the advocacy of the fourth item. The sixth item asked the governments of China and Japan to send high-ranking officials to negotiate the methods of withdrawing troops and receiving lost territory. The seventh item asked the governments of China and Japan to report the progress of the implementation of the resolution to the Executive Council at any time. The eighth item authorized the chairman to convene a meeting of the Executive Council when necessary to review the implementation of this resolution (to be continued).

Free Talk

Biography of General Teng 123

— Wang Zunchang

The Japanese disturbed Shanghai. Our dead numbered thousands. However, they also killed more than their due. Righteous voices moved heaven and earth. But the death of General Teng, Chief of Staff of the Wusong Fortress, was especially heroic. It was more than forty days after his death that it was heard outside. But the praise and comfort did not reach him. His wife and children had no way to protect themselves from the cold and hunger. The world heard and mourned him. General Teng's name was Jiu-shou, and his style name was Qi-zhi. He was from Dujiang County, Guizhou. He was brave and had integrity from a young age. In the eighth year of the Republic of China, he graduated from the Guizhou Army Lecture Hall and became the leader of a platoon in a certain army in Guizhou. He was repeatedly promoted to company commander, battalion commander, and regimental commander. In the fifteenth year, he entered Guangdong and was the main teacher at the Chaozhou Branch of the Central Military and Political School. The following year, he was the chief of staff of the Second Division of the Seventeenth Army. The following year, he was transferred to the chief of staff of the Twenty-ninth Division. He had meritorious service. In the winter of the eighteenth year, he was promoted to chief of staff of the Twenty-ninth Division. In the army, he was clearly different. He was strict in what he took and gave. He was ashamed of private fights. He only encouraged his subordinates to die for the country. His position rose day by day. People thought it was an honor. General Teng looked unhappy. When he heard that something had happened in the east, he often sighed. He became more and more self-disciplined. When the enemy invaded Shanghai, our Nineteenth Army was repeatedly defeated. The enemy then attacked Wusong with all their armor. The sound of artillery was heard for dozens of miles. The flames filled the sky. Wood and stone were all turned to ashes. People could not be seen five steps away. The fortress was in danger. General Teng received a letter to board the gun platform. Before he finished the steps, a bullet had hit his left arm. His clothes were all red. The crowd advised him to retreat. He refused. He fought hard despite his serious wounds. From morning to noon. The enemy was never able to succeed. Later, the artillery fire became more and more intense. A bullet pierced his left side. His upper body became minced meat. He then died for his country. It was the fourth day of the second month of the twenty-first year. He was only thirty-three years old. One hour after his death, we used a plan to cover up his main army. We shattered two enemy ships. The enemy was demoralized. Some said that it was General Teng's legacy.

Anecdotes from the Shanghai Battle 124

— Cai Liang

This battle in Shanghai was fierce. It was truly unprecedented since the opening of the port. And the loyalty and bravery of our army in resisting the enemy has also been made clear to the world. Here are some interesting things that were not published in the newspapers.

Eating rice and adding vinegar. My friend Mr. Wang used to live in Baoxing Road in northern Shanghai. His residence happened to be next to a certain Japanese person. According to him, several days before the incident, he saw the family buying a large number of red and green papers. They were cutting and making various lanterns and ornaments and were extremely busy. It was as if they were having a large-scale celebration. He was very confused. When Yan Ze launched an attack, and the overseas Chinese acted as his vanguard, he realized that these people had harbored evil intentions for a long time. Unexpectedly, after the first exchange of fire, they were defeated. Therefore, joy turned into sorrow. They fled in panic. Later, it was learned that these people were increasingly terrified by the casualties of the repeated battles and defeats. They also regarded it as a major national disaster. For a time, all the overseas Chinese ate vegetarian food to express their grief. It was also heard that they added a little vinegar when they ate, which was also what is called punishing themselves.

The Drama of Snatching Corpses. The initial battles took place in the Hongkou area. Therefore, the roads connected to the Chinese areas were the scene of fierce fighting. However, because the area was located in a city, there were many secluded alleys. The enemy was unfamiliar with the terrain. It was easy to attack but difficult to defend. Therefore, every time they were defeated, they left behind piles of corpses. The enemy was unwilling to abandon their dead soldiers. It was once heard that during one of our army's pursuits, we suddenly saw enemy sappers crawling in from the side. At first, we thought they were coming to help in the battle. Unexpectedly, when they approached the front line, they stopped. Then we saw these people frantically picking up their remains, flags, and other items. Our army immediately fired at them with machine guns. Most of them did not survive, it is said.

— Ping

The American intellectual class's movement to impose economic sanctions on Japan for using force to oppress China and disrupt world peace is beginning. Unfortunately, our people's work of resisting goods seems to be declining! At the same time, treacherous merchants in Tianjin and Qingdao are smuggling a large number of enemy goods. It is said that many have arrived in Shanghai. This tragic phenomenon is so disappointing and heartbreaking! In times of national crisis, there is only the common life and death of the entire nation. How can there be welfare for individuals and families? At this moment, regardless of the government's attitude, our people's determination to sacrifice for the country will never change! As for the methods of resisting goods, secret work is better than public activities. Our patriotic warriors, shop assistants, sailors, and customs officers should hold a spirit of great fearlessness, deeply monitor the actions of treacherous merchants, and take the most severe measures against them!

Short News The Parisian Dream. This is a famous French novel. The original name is Tender Love. It tells the love story of a writer and a singer. It is tragic and gentle. It will be screened at the Paris Grand Theatre starting on Friday.

The Battle of Shanghai and Military Weapons (4)

— Yi Zang

Machine Guns 126

Machine guns are divided into heavy and light types. Heavy machine guns were invented two hundred years after the invention of artillery. In 1400, there was something called Organs, which consisted of six or more and twenty or fewer gun barrels arranged side by side. In the sixteenth century, the Dutch created the harp cannon. During the Franco-Prussian War, the German army used this cannon, which was closely connected to twenty automatic rifles, for attack and defense. In 1860, the Gutoling machine gun was born. In 1883, the German Maxium invented the automatic machine gun. As a result, the technology shone brightly. German Emperor William I greatly appreciated it. At that time, our country's ambassador to Germany personally saw its ingenious structure. He personally tested it in Berlin. It was indeed fierce and unparalleled. He urgently wanted to purchase it, but he terminated the contract halfway because he thought the price of 200 yuan per piece was too expensive. This is the shortcoming of our people. Later, France invented the Hochiks automatic gas machine gun, which was even more fierce. During the Sino-Japanese War, Japan used Maxium machine guns to inflict its violence everywhere. At this time, our country only had a small number of local guns and old-fashioned rifles, so it could not resist. During the Russo-Japanese War, Japan also adopted the Hochiks automatic gas machine gun. When Yang Yuling was the general manager of the Northeast Arsenal, he hired German and French technicians to manufacture thousands of them. I don't know who has them now.

Records of Military Life in Twin Buildings (30) 127

— Master of the Studio of Seeking Happiness

Chapter 4: An Arranged Marriage Pressures Him, He Wanders in Doubt; Enemy Flames Burn the Land, A New Conflict Begins

Under such a state of infatuation, regarding the perfectly logical arranged marriage with Li Wenxia, he couldn't help but hesitate and feel extremely anxious. He tossed and turned all night, finally falling into a hazy sleep at dawn. He didn't know how long he had slept when he was suddenly awakened by the tea boy shouting loudly outside the window, saying that there was a phone call from the Liang residence for him. He hurriedly threw on his clothes and went out to answer the phone. It was Liang Xiaoyun speaking coquettishly on the phone, saying, "I've been up for half the day. Since you've been feeling unwell these past two days, you probably don't need to go to class. So, stop dawdling in the dormitory. Why aren't you coming over here?" He felt secretly ashamed that he was getting up later than a fashionable lady. What else could he say? He could only agree to come right away. After hanging up the receiver and running back to his room, he splashed water on his face haphazardly as if his eyebrows were on fire. He hurriedly put on a Western suit and, after finding the golden box, put it in his pocket. He no longer allowed himself any room for consideration or thought, nor did he have time to worry about the later appointment with Li Wenxia tonight. He only had one thing on his mind: getting to the Liang's house. As he walked to the door of the accounting office inside the dormitory gate, a postal messenger was delivering many letters. The accountant conveniently stopped him and handed him a letter. In his haste, he glanced at the envelope and recognized that it was sent by his uncle, An Dakui. However, it was not an express or registered letter. He guessed that there was no remittance inside, and he was slightly disappointed. He took the letter and ran out, jumping into a familiar rickshaw. He told the driver to go to the Liang's house. Only after the rickshaw reached the main street did he slowly open the letter to read it carefully. Who knew that it would have been better if he hadn't read it? Upon reading it, he was shocked and dismayed, experiencing another unexpected blow and feeling an extremely uncomfortable distress. He was stunned in the rickshaw for a moment. Unexpectedly, the rickshaw had already stopped in front of the Liang's house. In a daze, he got out of the rickshaw, paid the fare, and stuffed the letter into his pocket. Just as he was about to press the doorbell, he saw that the door of the Liang's house was already open. Outside the door, there was another hired car parked, which he recognized as the one used by Wei Zhuomou. The rickshaw driver and the doorman of the Liang's house were standing at the door chatting. When they saw him, a familiar acquaintance, they greeted him in unison. The doorman led him inside, smiling as he said, "Miss and Mr. Wei are both in the study." He went straight into the study and saw Liang Xiaoyun and Wei Zhuomou reading English at the desk.

The Situation of the Exchange Market Revolving 129

Long-Term News Is Bleak 132

In previous years, around early April, there would have been a small number of six-month long-term funds due today (the 10th), with various news of settlement, new transactions, and continuation. However, this time, there was no news at all. The reason for this is nothing more than the situation and market conditions. However, it was found that most of the long-term funds that expired at the end of last October failed to be repaid as desired. Instead, they were vaguely resolved with a plan to transfer to current accounts. It was expected that they could be cleared at the end of the year, but the national crisis of January 28th occurred, and the entire city was suspended. Subsequently, the deadline for completion was postponed several times, but no agreement was reached. It has not been resolved to this day. According to the notice from the City Chamber of Commerce, the overall deadline is the end of May. Therefore, the handling of long-term deposits, collections, and transfers in mid-April is difficult to manage. As a result, the usually good long-term news every year has become bleak and silent.

Wave Talk

Reply to Mr. Cai Linsheng's Letter 145

Mr. Linsheng,

Upon receiving and reading your letter, I was overjoyed beyond expectation. You instructed me to provide a certification and reply as soon as possible. I respectfully comply with your order and briefly describe one aspect, requesting your perusal.

When I was drafting the article, the sounds of cannons, airplanes, and bombs in Zhabei, Jiangwan, Wusong, and other places had subsided. However, the sounds of cannons, airplanes, and bombs in Jiading, Taicang, and other places rose again. Observing this war, the significant losses suffered by our side were due to airplanes and cannons. Among these two items, the bombs from airplanes were particularly fierce and frightening. Because the various destruction tragedies in Zhabei, Wusong, and other places were mostly caused by airplane bombs. This made me recall a news item that this newspaper once published: "Mr. Cai Linsheng, the inventor of our country's aerial thunder, has been summoned by the government to engage in manufacturing." Assuming that Mr. Cai had indeed invented this kind of weapon, then there would be no need to worry about the enemy's airplanes and bombs. However, this news item has been reported for a long time. Why is it that the destructive actions of the enemy's airplanes and bombs are becoming more and more intense, while the effectiveness of aerial thunder is silent and unknown? Furthermore, I think this kind of news may not be accurate. Newspaper news originally takes "recording what is heard" as its principle, so among the news disclosed every day, there are many that can be confirmed by facts, but it is also unavoidable that there are some that are not entirely true. Just like flying multiple kites can also obstruct the airplane's air route, this kind of fallacy is also published in newspapers. Citing proof is one example. Therefore, I deeply suspected that this news item was also not a true event. Moreover, in Zhabei, Wusong, and other places, news frequently spread about planes shot down after the battle, but it was never heard that any of them were shot down by Mr. Cai's aerial thunder. The facts were clear, and I dared not conceal them. Therefore, I suspected that Mr. Cai may not exist, and aerial thunder may not exist. My hope was so urgent that my conjecture was occasionally wrong. Explaining this in order to talk about it is the basis of my argument. However, in my haste and anger, my wording was rash and disrespectful to Xizi. I secretly apologize for this. However, the world is declining and turbulent, and noisy clamor is rampant. Often, words do not match actions, and actions do not match words. Boasting becomes a trend, and people exaggerate each other. But upon examining the facts, there is a vast difference. There are countless such people. Therefore, Confucius said, "Listen to their words, but also observe their actions," also fearing that hermits are mostly those who steal vain reputation. Since this was the case in ancient times, it is even more so now. This is why I do not dare to hastily recognize something as true before seeing it with my own eyes. This is also why my words are rebellious and reckless.

Unexpectedly, after reading your letter, I found that it was indeed the truth. I couldn't help but clap my hands in celebration and was filled with both gratitude and shame. When the country is in trouble, extraordinary talents emerge. We will all watch with anticipation as you defend the country and resist disaster. It is a great honor. As for the military and political department's presentation and the aviation administration's certificate, I think they were not made public at that time, and I had no way of knowing. Now, after reading your letter, I understand the inside story. The facts are not false, and it is clear and understandable. However, what I hope for and want to see is not official documents such as presentations and certificates. I deeply hope that the aerial thunder can have a significant effect and the greatest success so that all 400 million compatriots can benefit from your service. Then I will again carry thorns and confess my guilt at your door. I have briefly stated the outline, and I hope for your understanding. In haste, I am infinitely terrified. I respectfully reply,

Popular Literature and Art

Yan Guisheng's Death Affair Poem by Meng Shao'an 146

Guisheng, a Hunan native, was a lieutenant and attached platoon leader of the 7th Platoon, 3rd Battalion, 4th Regiment of the 19th Route Army. He died in battle on February 3rd on Yongxing Road, Shanghai. Every time he faced the enemy, he always led the charge, and the enemy scattered at the mere sight of him. During that battle, enemy soldiers fiercely charged our army's position from Yokohama Road and East Baoxing Road. He even took off his shirt, bared his chest, and used a machine gun to fight, shouting to kill the enemy, charging into the enemy lines. The enemy soldiers were so frightened that they collapsed and fled. Our frontline achieved a great victory, capturing seven enemy steel cannons and thirteen machine guns. The general was also struck by several bullets, yet still shouted, "Kill, kill, kill," advancing without stopping. He was truly a hero. His given name was Guisheng, his family name Yan. He was several feet tall with a heroic beard. He was familiar with tactics on and off the horse. The extraordinary essence of mountains and rivers resided in Xiangtan. He had experienced a hundred battles and dangers in half his life. His heart burned with the desire to wash away national humiliation. Although the enemy's atmosphere was evil, it could be overcome. He wished to stop the island bandits and bring peace to Jiangnan. He fought fiercely at the head of the river for ten days, and the enemy feared him like a roaring tiger. On February 3rd, poisonous fog filled the air. The battlefield was dark, and the sky was like ink. The enemy came like clouds, with both infantry and cavalry. Thunderous vehicles pressed down on the ground, towering high. He shouted loudly and tore his shirt, "What petty thieves dare to be so greedy? It is still easy for me to wipe you out before breakfast! Do not say that my blade is not sharp!" His chest was bare, his hair disheveled. He wielded an iron spear to drive away the ferocious brutes. Bullets flew from his hand faster than a sickle. Enemy soldiers were like grass, freely mowed down in one sweep. Our army followed, their horses unbridled, focused on charging into the enemy without looking back. The enemy's momentum collapsed like a crumbling cliff. In that battle, the enemy soldiers were completely annihilated. Only two or three survivors escaped. His body was also covered in a thousand wounds. Covered in blood, he fought even more fiercely. He would die for his country, and even death would be sweet. My strength is exhausted, my face covered in blood. He shouted loudly, baring his angry beard. Even as he died, he cursed the enemy incessantly. Alas, since the barbarian horses came trampling,

how can one bear to speak of the shattered mountains and rivers? The waters of the Liao River have turned blue. They seek to explore the thousand-mile gold city. Then they ascended the Great Wall, gazing menacingly like tigers. The armies abandoned their armor and fled in terrified panic. Yet there were also brave generals who could strategize, changing their allegiances and clinging to life shamelessly. Are they not seven-foot-tall men? How can they not feel ashamed when compared to Lord Yan? Only his body nourishes the eagles and vultures. Only his name is engraved in people's hearts. His heroic spirit in heaven is like a star toad, its light constantly shining on the peak of Mount Heng.

Peace Talks Written on March 25th by Zhuzun 147

The news of peace talks is spreading widely. Telegrams about troop deployments fly about in confusion. (Recent special reports in various newspapers say that Sichuan soldiers and Zhang Fakui's troops have set out to aid Shanghai) How many truly love their country? Are they not just seeking fame? They sit idly by and watch the opportunity slip away. (If the reinforcements had arrived when the 19th Route Army had not yet retreated, then Shanghai would not have fallen, and the battlefield would not have spread to Jiading and Taicang) Let us not make an alliance under the city walls. (Formal negotiations began on March 24th) Thousands of broken walls remain. One sorrows when facing the setting sun. (If the government truly signs a treaty that humiliates the nation in order to seek peace, then I ask, how will it face the tens of millions of families in Wusong and Zhabei whose homes have been destroyed?)

Popular Science

Gun Cotton Making 148

The warfare of the twentieth century is scientific. However, our country has never studied science. After the January 28th resistance against the enemy, we learned a good lesson and realized that our guns and cannons were far behind others. Therefore, we must now focus on science and use scientific methods to transform our guns and cannons. Now I will not talk about transformation, because I am not a scientist. What I will talk about is the most useful and important material in the manufacture of gunpowder: gun cotton. Now I will write it out for everyone to study together...

Gun cotton is made by soaking cotton in medicinal liquid. Its chemical formula is C6H7O2(NO3)3. If we want to make it roughly, we can use cotton waste from textile factories, plus one part nitric acid and three parts sulfuric acid, each placed in a pottery pot with a valve. Then slowly pour the nitric acid into the sulfuric acid, and use an iron rod to gradually mix them. Then cover the top. After several hours when it is completely cold, pour this mixed acid liquid into a pottery bowl of cold water. The bowl has an iron frame prepared in it. Soak the dried cotton waste (i.e., refined cotton) in this acid, and then stir it with an iron rod. Then drip the remaining acid on the iron frame. Repeat the soaking several times. The cotton consumes the acid, poured from the pot, while the cotton is being soaked. At this time, due to the action of nitric acid, a great heat is generated, so it must be cooled with cold water frequently. Most of the cotton in this bowl becomes roughly made gun cotton through this repeated soaking. After a few minutes, take it out with an iron hook. In this way, roughly made gun cotton is successfully produced.

Its shape and color are almost the same as refined cotton. However, once it is heated or impacted, it explodes immediately. Therefore, it occupies a very important and useful position in gunpowder.

Smelling Perfume Can Maintain Life: One Article 149

Professor Max Weston-Schiller of Columbia University recently reported on the relationship between perfume and vitamins at the New York Electrical Association, which has attracted the attention of the scientific community. He said that smelling high-quality perfume is almost equivalent to absorbing the efficacy of vitamin A. The fragrance in perfume contains chemically generated nutrients. Therefore, in the future, with the advancement of chemistry, it may be possible to maintain life by only smelling perfume without eating food. Although this theory has not yet been tested by society and cannot be believed to be true, from the perspective of the physiological effect of absorbing the same nutrients as vitamin D when ultraviolet rays are directly shone on the body, it is not unreasonable to believe that smelling perfume can generate vitamin A in the body. Therefore, it can be determined that this theory is not false with future advancement in chemistry.

Casual Chat

Enduring the Pain and Opening for Business 150

I remember when the sounds of gunfire and artillery fire filled Zhabei, I ran into a cloth store near my home to buy a few feet of coarse cloth. This "treasure house" was very big, as you could see from the fact that it occupied a long section of the street. Perhaps because of the "violent Japanese invasion and the suspension of business to resist humiliation," this "treasure house" only had two doors open, so naturally, buyers could enter and exit at will. Sure enough, "business was booming," with the air of "customers filling the hall." One of the shopkeepers was someone I knew, so I also politely greeted him as usual:

"How is business?" "So-so." "Oh? Then you haven't been affected by the war?" "Haha, if we can't open for business, how can we not be affected?"

"Ah!..."

Hmm, I understood that the so-called "suspension of business to resist humiliation" really caused them to suffer from the "violent Japanese invasion." So, in anger, I didn't buy any cloth and walked straight out. When I was walking out of the store, he pointed to a large container! of Japanese goods that had been sealed by a certain agency and said to me:

"Look, I really don't know when this big container of cloth can be unsealed."

I simply didn't have any appropriate words to answer him, so I walked onto the street dejectedly. These few words stayed with me. Today, because of my wife's nagging, I had to go and "patronize" his "treasure house" again. As I approached the door, I saw that the cloth store's doors were wide open, and a sign that read "Long-Term Resistance, Enduring the Pain and Opening for Business" had been put up on the wall. So I thought for sure that they wouldn't make things difficult for me today. Sure enough, as soon as I stepped into the store, the acquaintance called out to me from afar:

"Good morning!" So I also replied: "How is business?" "Yes, we opened for business yesterday!" He greeted me with a face full of smiles, even shaking my hand. He said:

"Spring has come, the sky is clear and it's getting warmer." So I catered to his psychology and said... "As long as the peace talks are successful, the world will be peaceful!"

Isn't that so? This is the patriotism of Chinese merchants!

Heart Dead at Cheng Yuan 151

Husband: "Staying at home all day, how boring! It's been two months, I'm so bored. I want to go for a stroll in the scenic West Lake. Can you accompany me?"

Wife: "I think so too, but I heard that peace is not very reliable. If we go to Hangzhou, wouldn't it be terrible if there were any disturbances? It's better to go to the park to breathe some fresh air. But I don't know if the park is open?"

Husband: "The park? It's been open for a long time. We could go for a walk after the 19th Route Army withdrew from Zhabei."

Wife: "Hongkou Park? Or the Bund Park?" Husband: "For something more luxurious and Westernized, Zhaofeng Park is good. It doesn't matter if we spend a few more coppers." Wife: "Okay, let's go!"

The Sino-Western Pharmacy on Fourth Malu The Sino-Western Pharmacy on Fourth Malu has reluctantly opened for business since the first of this month. It is manufacturing various spring and summer medicines day and night. Due to the war, a small number of wholesale customers from various provinces outside of Shanghai have had their shipments delayed, but they are now being routed around those areas and arriving without difficulty. Summer is approaching, and the pharmacy's "Old Brand Star Flower Water Perfume" can not only relieve odors, stop sweating, and prevent epidemics, but also treat all kinds of skin diseases. The volume of both retail and wholesale sales is increasing daily.

Letters 153

Letter from Xia Renjie Since your newspaper created this science column, I believe readers are extremely pleased. I have a request. Our country has suffered a terrible calamity at the hands of Japan this time, and everyone is deeply saddened by the "bombing by airplanes." Not only are the ruins of Zhabei all caused by aerial warfare, but also, according to the officers and soldiers on the front lines, everyone laments the great destructive power of airplanes, and our country can do nothing about it. Now, even the most foolish person is loudly shouting that there are only two ways to save the country: one is to promote aviation, and the other is to buy more anti-aircraft guns. There are now many patriotic people who want to donate money to help, but there is no one to make concrete suggestions, and furthermore, many people do not know the details of this matter. Therefore, I am writing to request that you collect detailed scientific information on both airplanes and anti-aircraft guns for us, and that you can awaken everyone to give practical support. Then, even though my power is weak, I will resolve to donate a few percent of my salary each month, or unite with like-minded people to raise funds to buy them. I respectfully wish you peace. Xia Renjie, fifth day of the month.
